<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">List of countries by carbon dioxide emissions per capita</h1> <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div> <div id="contentSub"></div>
<div id="jump-to-nav"></div> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
<div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CO2_per_capita_per_country.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="370" data-file-width="800" height="102" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/CO2_per_capita_per_country.png/220px-CO2_per_capita_per_country.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/CO2_per_capita_per_country.png/330px-CO2_per_capita_per_country.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/CO2_per_capita_per_country.png/440px-CO2_per_capita_per_country.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:CO2_per_capita_per_country.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>CO<sub>2</sub> emission per capita per year per country (2000 data)</div></div></div>
<p>This is a list of countries by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide_emissions" title="Carbon dioxide emissions">carbon dioxide emissions</a> emissions <a href="/wiki/Per_capita" title="Per capita">per capita</a> from 1990 through 2011. All data were calculated by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US_Department_of_Energy" title="US Department of Energy">US Department of Energy's</a> <a href="/wiki/Carbon_Dioxide_Information_Analysis_Center" title="Carbon Dioxide Information Analysis Center">Carbon Dioxide Information Analysis Center (CDIAC)</a>, mostly based on data collected from country agencies by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Statistics_Division" title="United Nations Statistics Division">United Nations Statistics Division</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> Countries are ranked by their <a href="/wiki/Tonne" title="Tonne">metric tonnes</a> of carbon dioxide emissions per capita in 2009. The data only consider carbon dioxide emissions from the burning of <a href="/wiki/Fossil_fuel" title="Fossil fuel">fossil fuels</a> and cement manufacture, but not emissions from land use such as <a href="/wiki/Deforestation" title="Deforestation">deforestation</a>. Emissions from international shipping or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bunker_fuels" title="Bunker fuels">bunker fuels</a> are also not included in national figures,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Schrooten2_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-Schrooten2-2">[2]</a></sup> which can make a significant difference for small countries with important ports.
</p><p>The carbon dioxide emissions of a country are only an indicator of one <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas" title="Greenhouse gas">greenhouse gas</a>. For a more complete idea of how a country influences <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a>, gases such as <a href="/wiki/Methane" title="Methane">methane</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nitrous_oxide" title="Nitrous oxide">nitrous oxide</a> should be taken into account. This is particularly so in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Agricultural" title="Agricultural">agricultural</a> economies.
</p><p>Carbon dioxide emissions are also known for earlier periods. A study of a global sample of twelve countries provide estimates for <span class="chemf nowrap">CO<span style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:-0.3em;vertical-align:-0.4em;line-height:1em;font-size:80%;text-align:left"><sup style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline"></sup><br/><sub style="font-size:inherit;line-height:inherit;vertical-align:baseline">2</sub></span></span> emissions since 1800 and explores the long-run drivers of carbon dioxide emissions by decomposing changes in carbon emissions into population, income, technological and energy mix changes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Drivers_of_Long-run_CO2_Emissions_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_Drivers_of_Long-run_CO2_Emissions-3">[3]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="toc" id="toc"><input class="toctogglecheckbox" id="toctogglecheckbox" role="button" style="display:none" type="checkbox"/><div class="toctitle" dir="ltr" lang="en"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>

</ul>
